weapons and Ukraine">Ukraine</a></dd></dl></td>\n</tr><tr><td style="text-align:right;font-size:115%"><div class="plainlinks hlist navbar mini"><ul><li class="nv-view"><a href="/wiki/Template:Nuclear_weapons" title="Template:Nuclear weapons"><abbr title="View this template">v</abbr></a></li><li class="nv-talk"><a href="/wiki/Template_talk:Nuclear_weapons" title="Template talk:Nuclear weapons"><abbr title="Discuss this template">t</abbr></a></li><li class="nv-edit"><a class="external text" href="//en.wikipedia.org/w/index.php?title=Template:Nuclear_weapons&amp;action=edit"><abbr title="Edit this template">e</abbr></a></li></ul></div></td></tr></tbody></table>\n<p>The United Kingdom was the third country to develop and test <a href="/wiki/Nuclear_weapons" class="mw-redirect" title="Nuclear weapons">nuclear weapons</a>, and is one of the <a href="/wiki/List_of_states_with_nuclear_weapons#Five_nuclear-weapon_states_under_the_NPT" title="List of states with nuclear weapons">five nuclear-weapon states</a> under the <a href="/wiki/Treaty_on_the_Non-Proliferation_of_Nuclear_Weapons" title="Treaty on the Non-Proliferation of Nuclear Weapons">Treaty on the Non-Proliferation of Nuclear Weapons</a>. The possession of nuclear weapons is an important component of Britain\'s national identity.\n</p><p>The UK initiated a nuclear weapons programme, codenamed <a href="/wiki/Tube_Alloys" title="Tube Alloys">Tube Alloys</a>, during the <a href="/wiki/Second_World_War" class="mw-redirect" title="Second World War">Second World War</a>. At the <a href="/wiki/Quebec_Conference,_1943" title="Quebec Conference, 1943">Quebec Conference</a> in August 1943, it was merged with the American <a href="/wiki/Manhattan_Project" title="Manhattan Project">Manhattan Project</a>. The <a href="/wiki/British_contribution_to_the_Manhattan_Project" title="British contribution to the Manhattan Project">British contribution to the Manhattan Project</a> saw British scientists participate in most of its work. The British government considered nuclear weapons to be a joint discovery, but the American <a href="/wiki/Atomic_Energy_Act_of_1946" title="Atomic Energy Act of 1946">Atomic Energy Act of 1946</a> (McMahon Act) restricted other countries, including the UK, from access to information about nuclear weapons. Fearing the loss of Britain\'s <a href="/wiki/Great_power" title="Great power">great power</a> status, the UK resumed its own project, now codenamed <a href="/wiki/High_Explosive_Research" title="High Explosive Research">High Explosive Research</a>. On 3 October 1952, it detonated an atomic bomb in the <a href="/wiki/Monte_Bello_Islands" class="mw-redirect" title="Monte Bello Islands">Monte Bello Islands</a> of <a href="/wiki/Western_Australia" title="Western Australia">Western Australia</a> in <a href="/wiki/Operation_Hurricane" title="Operation Hurricane">Operation Hurricane</a>. Eleven more British <a href="/wiki/Nuclear_weapons_tests_in_Australia" title="Nuclear weapons tests in Australia">nuclear weapons tests in Australia</a> were carried out over the following decade, including seven <a href="/wiki/British_nuclear_tests_at_Maralinga" title="British nuclear tests at Maralinga">British nuclear tests at Maralinga</a> in 1956 and 1957.\n</p><p>The <a href="/wiki/British_hydrogen_bomb_programme" title="British hydrogen bomb programme">British hydrogen bomb programme</a> demonstrated Britain\'s ability to produce <a href="/wiki/Thermonuclear_weapon" title="Thermonuclear weapon">thermonuclear weapons</a> in the <a href="/wiki/Operation_Grapple" title="Operation Grapple">Operation Grapple</a> nuclear tests in the Pacific, and led to the amendment of the McMahon Act. Since the <a href="/wiki/1958_US%E2%80%93UK_Mutual_Defence_Agreement" title="1958 US\xe2\x80\x93UK Mutual Defence Agreement">1958 US\xe2\x80\x93UK Mutual Defence Agreement</a>, the US and the UK have cooperated extensively on nuclear security matters. The nuclear <a href="/wiki/Special_Relationship" title="Special Relationship">Special Relationship</a> between the two countries has involved the exchange of <a href="/wiki/Classified_information" title="Classified information">classified</a> scientific data and <a href="/wiki/Fissile_material" title="Fissile material">fissile materials</a> such as <a href="/wiki/Uranium-235" title="Uranium-235">uranium-235</a> and <a href="/wiki/Plutonium" title="Plutonium">plutonium</a> The UK has not had a programme to develop an independent delivery system since the cancellation of the <a href="/wiki/Blue_Streak_(missile)" title="Blue Streak (missile)">Blue Streak</a> in 1960. Instead, it has purchased US delivery systems for UK use, fitting them with warheads designed and manufactured by the UK\'s <a href="/wiki/Atomic_Weapons_Establishment" title="Atomic Weapons Establishment">Atomic Weapons Establishment</a> (AWE) and its predecessor. Under the 1963, <a href="/wiki/Polaris_Sales_Agreement" title="Polaris Sales Agreement">Polaris Sales Agreement</a>, the US supplied the UK with <a href="/wiki/Polaris_missile" class="mw-redirect" title="Polaris missile">Polaris missiles</a> and <a href="/wiki/Nuclear_submarine" title="Nuclear submarine">nuclear submarine</a> technology. The US also supplied the RAF and <a href="/wiki/British_Army_of_the_Rhine" title="British Army of the Rhine">British Army of the Rhine</a> with nuclear weapons under <a href="/wiki/Project_E" title="Project E">Project E</a> until 1992. Nuclear-capable American aircraft have been based in the UK since 1949, but the last US nuclear weapons were withdrawn in 2006.\n</p><p>In 1982, the Polaris Sales Agreement was amended to allow the UK to purchase <a href="/wiki/UGM-133_Trident_II" title="UGM-133 Trident II">Trident II</a> missiles. Since 1998, when the UK decommissioned its tactical <a href="/wiki/WE.177" title="WE.177">WE.177</a> bombs, the <a href="/wiki/Trident_(UK_nuclear_programme)" title="Trident (UK nuclear programme)">Trident</a> has been the only operational nuclear weapons system in British service. The delivery system consists of four <a href="/wiki/Vanguard-class_submarine" title="Vanguard-class submarine"><i>Vanguard</i>-class</a> <a href="/wiki/Submarine" title="Submarine">submarine</a> based at <a href="/wiki/HMNB_Clyde" title="HMNB Clyde">HMNB Clyde</a> in Scotland. Each submarine is armed with up to sixteen <a href="/wiki/Trident_missile" class="mw-redirect" title="Trident missile">Trident II missiles</a>, each carrying warheads in up to eight <a href="/wiki/Multiple_independently_targetable_reentry_vehicle" title="Multiple independently targetable reentry vehicle">Multiple independently targetable reentry vehicles</a> (MIRVs). With at least one submarine always on patrol, the <i>Vanguards</i> perform a <a href="/wiki/Military_strategy" title="Military strategy">strategic</a> <a href="/wiki/Deterrence_theory" title="Deterrence theory">deterrence</a> role and also have a <a href="/wiki/Tactical_nuclear_weapon" title="Tactical nuclear weapon">sub-strategic</a> capability.\n</p>\n<div id="toc" class="toc"><input type="checkbox" role="button" id="toctogglecheckbox" class="toctogglecheckbox" style="display:none" /><div class="toctitle" lang="en" dir="ltr"><h2>Contents</h2><span href="#End_of_American_cooperation"><span class="tocnumber">1.3</span> <span class="toctext">End of American cooperation</span></a></li>\n<li class="toclevel-2 tocsection-5"><a href="#Resumption_of_independent_UK_efforts"><span class="tocnumber">1.4</span> <span class="toctext">Resumption of independent UK efforts</span></a></li>\n<li class="toclevel-2 tocsection-6"><a href="#Unsuccessful_attempt_to_renew_American_partnership"><span class="tocnumber">1.5</span> <span class="toctext">Unsuccessful attempt to renew American partnership</span></a></li>\n<li class="toclevel-2 tocsection-7"><a href="#First_test_and_early_systems"><span class="tocnumber">1.6</span> <span class="toctext">First test and early systems</span></a></li>\n<li class="toclevel-2 tocsection-8"><a href="#Thermonuclear_weaponry"><span class="tocnumber">1.7</span> <span class="toctext">Thermonuclear weaponry</span></a></li>\n<li class="toclevel-2 tocsection-9"><a href="#An_independent_deterrent"><span class="tocnumber">1.8</span> <span class="toctext">An independent deterrent</span></a></li>\n<li class="toclevel-2 tocsection-10"><a href="#Renewed_American_partnership"><span class="tocnumber">1.9</span> <span class="toctext">Renewed American partnership</span></a></li>\n<li class="toclevel-2 tocsection-11"><a href="#US_nuclear_weapons"><span class="tocnumber">1.10</span> <span class="toctext">US nuclear weapons</span></a></li>\n<li class="toclevel-2 tocsection-12"><a href="#British_nuclear_weapons"><span class="tocnumber">1.11</span> <span class="toctext">British nuclear weapons</span></a></li>\n<li class="toclevel-2 tocsection-13"><a href="#Polaris"><span class="tocnumber">1.12</span> <span class="toctext">Polaris</span></a></li>\n<li class="toclevel-2 tocsection-14"><a href="#Trident"><span class="tocnumber">1.13</span> <span class="toctext">Trident</span></a></li>\n<li class="toclevel-2 tocsection-15"><a href="#Trident_renewal"><span class="tocnumber">1.14</span> <span class="toctext">Trident renewal</span></a></li>\n</ul>\n</li>\n<li class="toclevel-1 tocsection-16"><a href="#Nuclear_tests"><span class="tocnumber">2</span> <span class="toctext">Nuclear tests</span></a></li>\n<li class="toclevel-1 tocsection-17"><a href="#US_nuclear_weapons_in_the_UK"><span class="tocnumber">3</span> <span class="toctext">US nuclear weapons in the UK</span></a></li>\n<li class="toclevel-1 tocsection-18"><a href="#Nuclear_defence"><span class="tocnumber">4</span> <span class="toctext">Nuclear defence</span></a>\n<ul>\n<li class="toclevel-2 tocsection-19"><a href="#Warning_systems"><span class="tocnumber">4.1</span> <span class="toctext">Warning systems</span></a></li>\n<li class="toclevel-2 tocsection-20"><a href="#Attack_scenarios"><span class="tocnumber">4.2</span> <span class="toctext">Attack scenarios</span></a></li>\n<li class="toclevel-2 tocsection-21"><a href="#Civil_defence"><span class="tocnumber">4.3</span> <span class="toctext">Civil defence</span></a></li>\n</ul>\n</li>\n<li class="toclevel-1 tocsection-22"><a href="#Research_and_production_facilities"><span class="tocnumber">5</span> <span class="toctext">Research and production facilities</span></a></li>\n<li class="toclevel-1 tocsection-23"><a href="#Anti-nuclear_movement"><span class="tocnumber">6</span> <span class="toctext">Anti-nuclear movement</span></a></li>\n<li class="toclevel-1 tocsection-24"><a href="#End_of_cross-party_support"><span class="tocnumber">7</span> <span class="toctext">End of cross-party support</span></a></li>\n<li class="toclevel-1 tocsection-25"><a href="#Nuclear_posture"><span class="tocnumber">8</span> <span class="toctext">Nuclear posture</span></a></li>\n<li class="toclevel-1 tocsection-26"><a href="#Nuclear_weapons_control"><span class="tocnumber">9</span> <span class="toctext">Nuclear weapons control</span></a></li>\n<li class="toclevel-1 tocsection-27"><a href="#Legality"><span class="tocnumber">10</span> <span class="toctext">Legality</span></a></li>\n<li class="toclevel-1 tocsection-28"><a href="#Notes"><span class="tocnumber">11</span> <span class="toctext">Notes</span></a></li>\n<li class="toclevel-1 tocsection-29"><a href="#References"><span class="tocnumber">12</span> <span class="toctext">References</span></a></li>\n<li class="toclevel-1 tocsection-30"><a href="#External_links"><span class="tocnumber">13</span> <span class="toctext">External links</span></a></li>\n</ul>\n</div>\n\n<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="History">History</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Nuclear_weapons_and_the_United_Kingdom&amp;action=edit&amp;section=1" title="Edit section: History">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>\n<div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">Further information: <a href="/wiki/History_of_nuclear_weapons" title="History of nuclear weapons">History of nuclear weapons</a></div>\n<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Tube_Alloys">Tube Alloys</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Nuclear_weapons_and_the_United_Kingdom&amp;action=edit&amp;section=2" title="Edit section: Tube Alloys">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>\n<div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">Main articles: <a href="/wiki/MAUD_Committee" title="MAUD Committee">MAUD Committee</a> and <a href="/wiki/Tube_Alloys" title="Tube Alloys">Tube Alloys</a></div>\n<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Poynting_Physics_building_1.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/7/7d/Poynting_Physics_building_1.jpg/220px-Poynting_Physics_building_1.jpg" width="220" height="165" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/7/7d/Poynting_Physics_building_1.jpg/330px-Poynting_Physics_building_1.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/7/7d/Poynting_Physics_building_1.jpg/440px-Poynting_Physics_building_1.jpg 2x" data-file-width="3264" data-file-height="2448" /></a>  <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Poynting_Physics_building_1.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>The <a href="/wiki/John_Henry_Poynting" title="John Henry Poynting">Poynting</a> Physics building at the <a href="/wiki/University_of_Birmingham" title="University of Birmingham">University of Birmingham</a>, where Peierls and Frisch wrote the <a href="/wiki/Frisch%E2%80%93Peierls_memorandum" title="Frisch\xe2\x80\x93Peierls memorandum">Frisch\xe2\x80\x93Peierls memorandum</a></div></div></div>\n<p>The <a href="/wiki/Neutron" title="Neutron">neutron</a> was discovered by <a href="/wiki/James_Chadwick" title="James Chadwick">James Chadwick</a> at the <a href="/wiki/Cavendish_Laboratory" title="Cavendish Laboratory">Cavendish Laboratory</a> at the <a href="/wiki/University_of_Cambridge" title="University of Cambridge">University of Cambridge</a> in February 1932,<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEClark19619_1-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEClark19619-1">&#91;1&#93;</a></sup> and in April 1932, his Cavendish colleagues <a href="/wiki/John_Cockcroft" title="John Cockcroft">John Cockcroft</a> and <a href="/wiki/Ernest_Walton" title="Ernest Walton">Ernest Walton</a> split <a href="/wiki/Lithium" title="Lithium">lithium</a> atoms with accelerated <a href="/wiki/Proton" title="Proton">protons</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEGowing196417\xe2\x80\x9318_2-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEGowing196417\xe2\x80\x9318-2">&#91;2&#93;</a></sup> In December 1938, <a href="/wiki/Otto_Hahn" title="Otto Hahn">Otto Hahn</a> and <a href="/wiki/Fritz_Strassmann" title="Fritz Strassmann">Fritz Strassmann</a> at Hahn\'s laboratory in <a href="/wiki/Berlin-Dahlem" class="mw-redirect" title="Berlin-Dahlem">Berlin-Dahlem</a> bombarded <a href="/wiki/Uranium" title="Uranium">uranium</a> with slow neutrons,<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEClark19615_3-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEClark19615-3">&#91;3&#93;</a></sup> and discovered that <a href="/wiki/Barium" title="Barium">barium</a> had been produced.<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEClark196111_4-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEClark196111-4">&#91;4&#93;</a></sup> Hahn wrote to his colleague <a href="/wiki/Lise_Meitner" title="Lise Meitner">Lise Meitner</a>, who, with her nephew <a href="/wiki/Otto_Frisch" class="mw-redirect" title="Otto Frisch">Otto Frisch</a>, who determined that the uranium <a href="/wiki/Atomic_nucleus" title="Atomic nucleus">nucleus</a> had been split, a conclusion they published in <i><a href="/wiki/Nature_(journal)" title="Nature (journal)">Nature</a></i> in 1939.<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEBernstein2011240_5-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEBernstein2011240-5">&#91;5&#93;</a></sup> By analogy with the <a href="/wiki/Fission_(biology)" title="Fission (biology)">division of biological cells</a>, they named the process "<a href="/wiki/Nuclear_fission" title="Nuclear fission">fission</a>".<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEZimmerman1995262_6-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEZimmerman1995262-6">&#91;6&#93;</a></sup>\n</p><p>The discovery of fission raised the possibility that an extremely powerful <a href="/wiki/Atomic_bomb" class="mw-redirect" title="Atomic bomb">atomic bomb</a> could be created.<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEGowing196423\xe2\x80\x9329_7-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEGowing196423\xe2\x80\x9329-7">&#91;7&#93;</a></sup> The term was already familiar to the British public through the writings of <a href="/wiki/H._G._Wells" title="H. G. Wells">H. G. Wells</a>, with a continuously-exploding bomb in his 1913 novel <i><a href="/wiki/The_World_Set_Free" title="The World Set Free">The World Set Free</a></i>.<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEFarmelo201315\xe2\x80\x9324_8-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEFarmelo201315\xe2\x80\x9324-8">&#91;8&#93;</a></sup> <a href="/wiki/George_Paget_Thomson" title="George Paget Thomson">George Paget Thomson</a>, at <a href="/wiki/Imperial_College_London" title="Imperial College London">Imperial College London</a>, and <a href="/wiki/Mark_Oliphant" title="Mark Oliphant">Mark Oliphant</a>, an Australian physicist at the <a href="/wiki/University_of_Birmingham" title="University of Birmingham">University of Birmingham</a>, were tasked with carrying out a series of experiments on uranium.<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEGowing196437\xe2\x80\x9339_9-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEGowing196437\xe2\x80\x9339-9">&#91;9&#93;</a></sup> Oliphant delegated the task to two German refugee scientists, <a href="/wiki/Rudolf_Peierls" title="Rudolf Peierls">Rudolf Peierls</a> and Frisch, who ironically could not work on the university\'s secret projects like <a href="/wiki/Radar" title="Radar">radar</a> because they were <a href="/wiki/Enemy_alien" title="Enemy alien">enemy aliens</a> and therefore lacked the necessary security clearance.<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTESzasz19923\xe2\x80\x935_10-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTESzasz19923\xe2\x80\x935-10">&#91;10&#93;</a></sup> They calculated the <a href="/wiki/Critical_mass" title="Critical mass">critical mass</a> of a metallic sphere of pure <a href="/wiki/Uranium-235" title="Uranium-235">uranium-235</a>, and found that instead of tons, as everyone had assumed, as little as 1 to 10 kilograms (2.2 to 22.0&#160;lb) would suffice, which would explode with the power of thousands of tons of dynamite.<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEGowing196439\xe2\x80\x9341_11-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEGowing196439\xe2\x80\x9341-11">&#91;11&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEBernstein2011440\xe2\x80\x93446_12-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEBernstein2011440\xe2\x80\x93446-12">&#91;12&#93;</a></sup>\n</p><p>Oliphant took the <a href="/wiki/Frisch%E2%80%93Peierls_memorandum" title="Frisch\xe2\x80\x93Peierls memorandum">Frisch\xe2\x80\x93Peierls memorandum</a> to Sir <a href="/wiki/Henry_Tizard" title="Henry Tizard">Henry Tizard</a>, the chairman of the <a href="/wiki/Tizard_Committee" class="mw-redirect" title="Tizard Committee">Tizard Committee</a>,<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEClark196154\xe2\x80\x9356_13-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEClark196154\xe2\x80\x9356-13">&#91;13&#93;</a></sup> and the <a href="/wiki/MAUD_Committee" title="MAUD Committee">MAUD Committee</a> was established to investigate further.<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEHewlettAnderson196239\xe2\x80\x9340_14-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEHewlettAnderson196239\xe2\x80\x9340-14">&#91;14&#93;</a></sup> It directed an intensive research effort, and in July 1941, produced two comprehensive reports that reached the conclusion that an atomic bomb was not only technically feasible, but could be produced before the war ended, perhaps in as little as two years. The Committee unanimously recommended pursuing the development of an atomic bomb as a matter of urgency, although it recognised that the resources required might be beyond those available to Britain.<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEPhelps2010282\xe2\x80\x93283_15-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEPhelps2010282\xe2\x80\x93283-15">&#91;15&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEHewlettAnderson196242_16-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEHewlettAnderson196242-16">&#91;16&#93;</a></sup> A new directorate known as <a href="/wiki/Tube_Alloys" title="Tube Alloys">Tube Alloys</a> was created to coordinate this effort. Sir <a href="/wiki/John_Anderson,_1st_Viscount_Waverley" title="John Anderson, 1st Viscount Waverley">John Anderson</a>, the <a href="/wiki/Lord_President_of_the_Council" title="Lord President of the Council">Lord President of the Council</a>, became the minister responsible, and <a href="/wiki/Wallace_Akers" title="Wallace Akers">Wallace Akers</a> from <a href="/wiki/Imperial_Chemical_Industries" title="Imperial Chemical Industries">Imperial Chemical Industries</a> (ICI) was appointed the director of Tube Alloys.<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEGowing1964108\xe2\x80\x93111_17-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEGowing1964108\xe2\x80\x93111-17">&#91;17&#93;</a></sup>\n</p>\n<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Manhattan_Project">Manhattan Project</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Nuclear_weapons_and_the_United_Kingdom&amp;action=edit&amp;section=3" title="Edit section: Manhattan Project">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>\n<div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">Main article: <a href="/wiki/British_contribution_to_the_Manhattan_Project" title="British contribution to the Manhattan Project">British contribution to the Manhattan Project</a></div>\n<p>In July 1940, Britain had offered to give the United States access to its scientific research,<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEPhelps2010126\xe2\x80\x93128_18-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEPhelps2010126\xe2\x80\x93128-18">&#91;18&#93;</a></sup> and the <a href="/wiki/Tizard_Mission" title="Tizard Mission">Tizard Mission</a>\'s John Cockcroft briefed American scientists on British developments.<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEZimmerman1995266\xe2\x80\x93267_19-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEZimmerman1995266\xe2\x80\x93267-19">&#91;19&#93;</a></sup> He discovered that the American S-1 Project (later renamed the <a href="/wiki/Manhattan_Project" title="Manhattan Project">Manhattan Project</a>) was smaller than the British, and not as far advanced.<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEPhelps2010282\xe2\x80\x93283_15-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEPhelps2010282\xe2\x80\x93283-15">&#91;15&#93;</a></sup> The British and American projects exchanged information, but did not initially combine their efforts. British officials did not reply to an August 1941 American offer to create a combined project.<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEBernstein1976206\xe2\x80\x93207_20-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEBernstein1976206\xe2\x80\x93207-20">&#91;20&#93;</a></sup> In November 1941, <a href="/wiki/Frederick_L._Hovde" title="Frederick L. Hovde">Frederick L. Hovde</a>, the head of the London liaison office of the American <a href="/wiki/Office_of_Scientific_Research_and_Development" title="Office of Scientific Research and Development">Office of Scientific Research and Development</a> (OSRD), raised the issue of cooperation and exchange of information with Anderson and <a href="/wiki/Lord_Cherwell" class="mw-redirect" title="Lord Cherwell">Lord Cherwell</a>, who demurred, ostensibly over concerns about American security. Ironically, it was the British project that had already been penetrated by <a href="/wiki/Atomic_spies" title="Atomic spies">atomic spies</a> for the <a href="/wiki/Soviet_Union" title="Soviet Union">Soviet Union</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEPaul200026_21-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEPaul200026-21">&#91;21&#93;</a></sup>\n</p>\n<div class="thumb tleft"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Groves_and_Chadwick_830308.jpg" class="image"><img alt="A large man in uniform and a bespectacled thin man in a suit and tie sit at a desk." src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/5/56/Groves_and_Chadwick_830308.jpg/220px-Groves_and_Chadwick_830308.jpg" width="220" height="166" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/5/56/Groves_and_Chadwick_830308.jpg/330px-Groves_and_Chadwick_830308.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/5/56/Groves_and_Chadwick_830308.jpg/440px-Groves_and_Chadwick_830308.jpg 2x" data-file-width="3000" data-file-height="2269" /></a>  <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Groves_and_Chadwick_830308.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div><a href="/wiki/James_Chadwick" title="James Chadwick">James Chadwick</a> (left), the head of the British Mission, confers with <a href="/wiki/Major_general_(United_States)" title="Major general (United States)">Major General</a> <a href="/wiki/Leslie_R._Groves,_Jr." class="mw-redirect" title="Leslie R. Groves, Jr.">Leslie R. Groves, Jr.</a> (right), the director of the <a href="/wiki/Manhattan_Project" title="Manhattan Project">Manhattan Project</a></div></div></div>\n<p>The United Kingdom did not have the manpower or resources of the United States, and despite its early and promising start, Tube Alloys fell behind its American counterpart and was dwarfed by it.<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEBernstein1976206\xe2\x80\x93208_22-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEBernstein1976206\xe2\x80\x93208-22">&#91;22&#93;</a></sup> On 30 July 1942, Anderson advised  the <a href="/wiki/Prime_Minister_of_the_United_Kingdom" title="Prime Minister of the United Kingdom">Prime Minister</a>, <a href="/wiki/Winston_Churchill" title="Winston Churchill">Winston Churchill</a>, that: "We must face the fact that&#160;... [our] pioneering work&#160;... is a dwindling asset and that, unless we capitalise it quickly, we shall be outstripped. We now have a real contribution to make to a \'merger.\' Soon we shall have little or none."<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEBernstein1976208_23-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEBernstein1976208-23">&#91;23&#93;</a></sup>\n</p><p>The British considered producing an atomic bomb without American help, but it would require overwhelming priority, disruption to other wartime projects was inevitable, and it was unlikely to be ready in time to affect the outcome of the <a href="/wiki/European_Theatre_of_World_War_II" class="mw-redirect" title="European Theatre of World War II">war in Europe</a>. The unanimous response was that before embarking on this, another effort should be made to secure American cooperation.<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEGowing1964162\xe2\x80\x93165_24-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEGowing1964162\xe2\x80\x93165-24">&#91;24&#93;</a></sup> At the <a href="/wiki/Quebec_Conference,_1943" title="Quebec Conference, 1943">Quebec Conference</a> in August 1943, Churchill and the <a href="/wiki/President_of_the_United_States" title="President of the United States">President of the United States</a>, <a href="/wiki/Franklin_Roosevelt" class="mw-redirect" title="Franklin Roosevelt">Franklin Roosevelt</a>, signed the <a href="/wiki/Quebec_Agreement" title="Quebec Agreement">Quebec Agreement</a>, which merged the two national projects.<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEHewlettAnderson1962277_25-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEHewlettAnderson1962277-25">&#91;25&#93;</a></sup> The Quebec Agreement established the <a href="/wiki/Combined_Policy_Committee" class="mw-redirect" title="Combined Policy Committee">Combined Policy Committee</a> and the <a href="/wiki/Combined_Development_Trust" class="mw-redirect" title="Combined Development Trust">Combined Development Trust</a> to coordinate their efforts, and specified that the weapons could only be used if both the USA and UK governments agreed.<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEHewlettAnderson1962285\xe2\x80\x93286_26-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEHewlettAnderson1962285\xe2\x80\x93286-26">&#91;26&#93;</a></sup> The 19 September 1944 Hyde Park Agreement extended both commercial and military cooperation into the post-war period.<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEGowing1964340\xe2\x80\x93342_27-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEGowing1964340\xe2\x80\x93342-27">&#91;27&#93;</a></sup>\n</p><p>A British mission led by Akers assisted in the development of <a href="/wiki/Gaseous_diffusion" title="Gaseous diffusion">gaseous diffusion</a> technology at the <a href="/wiki/SAM_Laboratories" class="mw-redirect" title="SAM Laboratories">SAM Laboratories</a> in New York.<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEGowing1964250\xe2\x80\x93256_28-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEGowing1964250\xe2\x80\x93256-28">&#91;28&#93;</a></sup> Another, led by Oliphant, who acted as deputy director at the <a href="/wiki/Berkeley_Radiation_Laboratory" class="mw-redirect" title="Berkeley Radiation Laboratory">Berkeley Radiation Laboratory</a>, assisted with the <a href="/wiki/Electromagnetic_separation" class="mw-redirect" title="Electromagnetic separation">electromagnetic separation</a> process.<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEGowing1964226\xe2\x80\x93227,_256\xe2\x80\x93258_29-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEGowing1964226\xe2\x80\x93227,_256\xe2\x80\x93258-29">&#91;29&#93;</a></sup> Cockcroft became the director of the Anglo-Canadian <a href="/wiki/Montreal_Laboratory" title="Montreal Laboratory">Montreal Laboratory</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEJones1985246\xe2\x80\x93247_30-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEJones1985246\xe2\x80\x93247-30">&#91;30&#93;</a></sup> The British mission to the <a href="/wiki/Los_Alamos_Laboratory" class="mw-redirect" title="Los Alamos Laboratory">Los Alamos Laboratory</a> was headed by Chadwick, and later Peierls. It included distinguished scientists such as <a href="/wiki/G._I._Taylor" title="G. I. Taylor">Geoffrey Taylor</a>, <a href="/wiki/James_L._Tuck" title="James L. Tuck">James Tuck</a>, <a href="/wiki/Niels_Bohr" title="Niels Bohr">Niels Bohr</a>, <a href="/wiki/William_George_Penney" class="mw-redirect" title="William George Penney">William Penney</a>, Frisch, <a href="/wiki/Ernest_Titterton" title="Ernest Titterton">Ernest Titterton</a> and <a href="/wiki/Klaus_Fuchs" title="Klaus Fuchs">Klaus Fuchs</a>, who was later revealed to be a Soviet spy.<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTESzasz1992148\xe2\x80\x93151_31-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTESzasz1992148\xe2\x80\x93151-31">&#91;31&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEGowing1964260\xe2\x80\x93268_32-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEGowing1964260\xe2\x80\x93268-32">&#91;32&#93;</a></sup> As overall head of the British Mission, Chadwick forged a close and successful partnership with <a href="/wiki/Brigadier_general_(United_States)" title="Brigadier general (United States)">Brigadier General</a> <a href="/wiki/Leslie_R._Groves" class="mw-redirect" title="Leslie R. Groves">Leslie R. Groves</a>, the director of the Manhattan Project.<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEGowing1964236\xe2\x80\x93239_33-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEGowing1964236\xe2\x80\x93239-33">&#91;33&#93;</a></sup> He ensured that British participation was complete and wholehearted.<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEGowing1964242_34-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEGowing1964242-34">&#91;34&#93;</a></sup>\n</p><p>Penney worked on means to assess the effects of a nuclear explosion, and wrote a paper on what height the bombs should be detonated at for maximum effect in attacks on Germany and Japan.<sup id="cite_ref-35" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-35">&#91;35&#93;</a></sup> He served as a member of the target committee established by Groves to select Japanese cities for atomic bombing,<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEJones1985528_36-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEJones1985528-36">&#91;36&#93;</a></sup> and on <a href="/wiki/Tinian" title="Tinian">Tinian</a> with <a href="/wiki/Project_Alberta" title="Project Alberta">Project Alberta</a> as a special consultant.<sup id="cite_ref-Roster_37-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Roster-37">&#91;37&#93;</a></sup> Because the Quebec Agreement specified that nuclear weapons would not be used against another country without mutual consent, British authorisation was required for their use. On 4 July 1945, Wilson agreed that the use of nuclear weapons against Japan would be recorded as a decision of the Combined Policy Committee.<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEGowing1964372_38-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEGowing1964372-38">&#91;38&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEHewlettAnderson1962372\xe2\x80\x93373_39-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEHewlettAnderson1962372\xe2\x80\x93373-39">&#91;39&#93;</a></sup> Along with <a href="/wiki/Group_Captain" class="mw-redirect" title="Group Captain">Group Captain</a> <a href="/wiki/Leonard_Cheshire" title="Leonard Cheshire">Leonard Cheshire</a>, sent by Wilson as a British representative, Penney watched the <a href="/wiki/Bombing_of_Nagasaki" class="mw-redirect" title="Bombing of Nagasaki">bombing of Nagasaki</a> from the observation plane <i><a href="/wiki/Big_Stink_(B-29)" class="mw-redirect" title="Big Stink (B-29)">Big Stink</a></i>.<sup id="cite_ref-eyewitness_40-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-eyewitness-40">&#91;40&#93;</a></sup> He also formed part of the Manhattan Project\'s post-war scientific mission to Hiroshima and Nagasaki that assessed the extent of the damage caused by the bombs.<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTESzasz199264_41-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTESzasz199264-41">&#91;41&#93;</a></sup>\n</p>\n<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="End_of_American_cooperation">End of American cooperation</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Nuclear_weapons_and_the_United_Kingdom&amp;action=edit&amp;section=4" title="Edit section: End of American cooperation">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>\n<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a href="/wiki/File:TrumanAttleeKing1945.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/0/03/TrumanAttleeKing1945.jpg/220px-TrumanAttleeKing1945.jpg" width="220" height="175" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/0/03/TrumanAttleeKing1945.jpg/330px-TrumanAttleeKing1945.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/0/03/TrumanAttleeKing1945.jpg/440px-TrumanAttleeKing1945.jpg 2x" data-file-width="597" data-file-height="474" /></a>  <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:TrumanAttleeKing1945.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>President <a href="/wiki/Harry_Truman" class="mw-redirect" title="Harry Truman">Harry Truman</a> and prime ministers <a href="/wiki/Clement_Attlee" title="Clement Attlee">Clement Attlee</a> and <a href="/wiki/Mackenzie_King" class="mw-redirect" title="Mackenzie King">Mackenzie King</a> boarding <a href="/wiki/USS_Sequoia_(presidential_yacht)" title="USS Sequoia (presidential yacht)">USS&#160;<i>Sequoia</i></a> for discussions about nuclear weapons, November 1945</div></div></div>\n<p>With the end of the war, the <a href="/wiki/Special_Relationship" title="Special Relationship">Special Relationship</a> between Britain and the United States "became very much less special".<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEGowingArnold1974a93_42-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEGowingArnold1974a93-42">&#91;42&#93;</a></sup> The British government had trusted that America would share nuclear technology, which it considered a joint discovery.<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEGoldberg1964410_43-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEGoldberg1964410-43">&#91;43&#93;</a></sup> On 8 August 1945  the Prime Minister, <a href="/wiki/Clement_Attlee" title="Clement Attlee">Clement Attlee</a>, sent a message to President <a href="/wiki/Harry_Truman" class="mw-redirect" title="Harry Truman">Harry Truman</a> in which he referred to themselves as "heads of the Governments which have control of this great force".<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEGoldberg1964410_43-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEGoldberg1964410-43">&#91;43&#93;</a></sup> But Roosevelt had died on 12 April 1945, and the Hyde Park Agreement was not binding on subsequent administrations.<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEPaul200072\xe2\x80\x9373_44-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEPaul200072\xe2\x80\x9373-44">&#91;44&#93;</a></sup> In fact, it was physically lost. When Wilson raised the matter in a Combined Policy Committee meeting in June, the American copy could not be found.<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEHewlettAnderson1962457\xe2\x80\x93458_45-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEHewlettAnderson1962457\xe2\x80\x93458-45">&#91;45&#93;</a></sup>\n</p><p>On 9 November 1945, Attlee and the <a href="/wiki/Prime_Minister_of_Canada" title="Prime Minister of Canada">Prime Minister of Canada</a>, <a href="/wiki/Mackenzie_King" class="mw-redirect" title="Mackenzie King">Mackenzie King</a>, went to Washington, D.C., to confer with Truman about future cooperation in nuclear weapons and nuclear power.<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEGott1963240_46-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEGott1963240-46">&#91;46&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEGowingArnold1974a73\xe2\x80\x9377_47-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEGowingArnold1974a73\xe2\x80\x9377-47">&#91;47&#93;</a></sup> A Memorandum of Intention they signed replaced the Quebec Agreement. It made Canada a full partner, continued the Combined Policy Committee and Combined Development Trust, and reduced the obligation to obtain consent for the use of nuclear weapons to merely requiring consultation.<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEHewlettAnderson1962468_48-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEHewlettAnderson1962468-48">&#91;48&#93;</a></sup> The three leaders agreed that there would be full and effective cooperation on atomic energy, but British hopes were soon disappointed;<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEGowingArnold1974a92_49-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEGowingArnold1974a92-49">&#91;49&#93;</a></sup> the Americans restricted  cooperation to basic scientific research.<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEPaul200080\xe2\x80\x9383_50-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEPaul200080\xe2\x80\x9383-50">&#91;50&#93;</a></sup>\n</p><p>The next meeting of the Combined Policy Committee on 15 April 1946 produced no accord on collaboration, and resulted in an exchange of cables between Truman and Attlee. Truman cabled on 20 April that he did not see the communiqu\xc3\xa9 he had signed as obligating the United States to assist Britain in designing, constructing and operating an atomic energy plant.<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEPaul200088_51-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEPaul200088-51">&#91;51&#93;</a></sup> The passing of the <a href="/wiki/Atomic_Energy_Act_of_1946" title="Atomic Energy Act of 1946">Atomic Energy Act of 1946</a> (McMahon Act) in August 1946, which was signed by Truman on 1 August 1946, and went into effect at midnight on 1 January 1947,<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEJones1985576\xe2\x80\x93578_52-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEJones1985576\xe2\x80\x93578-52">&#91;52&#93;</a></sup> ended technical cooperation. Its control of "restricted data" prevented the United States\' allies from receiving any information.<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEGowingArnold1974a106\xe2\x80\x93108_53-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEGowingArnold1974a106\xe2\x80\x93108-53">&#91;53&#93;</a></sup> The remaining British scientists working in the United States were denied access to papers that they had written just days before.<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEFarmelo2013322_54-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEFarmelo2013322-54">&#91;54&#93;</a></sup>\n</p><p>This partly resulted from the arrest for espionage of British physicist <a href="/wiki/Alan_Nunn_May" title="Alan Nunn May">Alan Nunn May</a>, who had worked in the Montreal Laboratory, in February 1946, while the legislation was being debated.<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEGowingArnold1974a105\xe2\x80\x93108_55-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEGowingArnold1974a105\xe2\x80\x93108-55">&#91;55&#93;</a></sup> It was but the first of a series of spy scandals. The arrest of Klaus Fuchs in January 1950,<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEBotti198761_56-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEBotti198761-56">&#91;56&#93;</a></sup> and the June 1951 defection of <a href="/wiki/Donald_Maclean_(spy)" title="Donald Maclean (spy)">Donald Maclean</a>, who had served as a British member of the Combined Policy Committee from January 1947 to August 1948, left Americans with a distrust of British security arrangements.<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEBotti198774\xe2\x80\x9375_57-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEBotti198774\xe2\x80\x9375-57">&#91;57&#93;</a></sup>\n</p>\n<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Resumption_of_independent_UK_efforts">Resumption of independent UK efforts</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Nuclear_weapons_and_the_United_Kingdom&amp;action=edit&amp;section=5" title="Edit section: Resumption of independent UK efforts">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>\n<div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">Main article: <a href="/wiki/High_Explosive_Research" title="High Explosive Research">High Explosive Research</a></div>\n<p>Attlee set up a <a href="/wiki/United_Kingdom_cabinet_committee" title="United Kingdom cabinet committee">cabinet sub-committee</a>, the <a href="/wiki/Gen_75_Committee" title="Gen 75 Committee">Gen 75 Committee</a> (known informally by Attlee as the "Atomic Bomb Committee"),<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEGowingArnold1974a21_58-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEGowingArnold1974a21-58">&#91;58&#93;</a></sup> on 10 August 1945 to examine the feasibility of an independent British nuclear weapons programme.<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEBaylisStoddart201532_59-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEBaylisStoddart201532-59">&#91;59&#93;</a></sup> The <a href="/wiki/Chiefs_of_Staff_Committee" title="Chiefs of Staff Committee">Chiefs of Staff Committee</a> considered the issue of nuclear weapons in July 1946, and recommended that Britain acquire them.<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEWynn199716\xe2\x80\x9318_60-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEWynn199716\xe2\x80\x9318-60">&#91;60&#93;</a></sup> The <a href="/wiki/Chief_of_the_Air_Staff_(United_Kingdom)" title="Chief of the Air Staff (United Kingdom)">Chief of the Air Staff</a>, <a href="/wiki/Marshal_of_the_Royal_Air_Force" title="Marshal of the Royal Air Force">Marshal of the Royal Air Force</a> <a href="/wiki/Arthur_Tedder,_1st_Baron_Tedder" title="Arthur Tedder, 1st Baron Tedder">Lord Tedder</a>, officially requested an atomic bomb in 9 August 1946.<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEGowingArnold1974a174_61-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEGowingArnold1974a174-61">&#91;61&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEWynn19976,_18_62-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEWynn19976,_18-62">&#91;62&#93;</a></sup> The Chiefs of Staff estimated that 200 bombs would be required by 1957.<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEGowingArnold1974a216_63-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEGowingArnold1974a216-63">&#91;63&#93;</a></sup> A <a href="/wiki/Nuclear_reactor" title="Nuclear reactor">nuclear reactor</a> and <a href="/wiki/Plutonium" title="Plutonium">plutonium</a>-processing facility was approved by the Gen 75 committee on 18 December 1945 "with the highest urgency and importance".<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEWynn199711\xe2\x80\x9312_64-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEWynn199711\xe2\x80\x9312-64">&#91;64&#93;</a></sup>\n</p>\n<div class="thumb tleft"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:172px;"><a href="/wiki/File:William_Penney_portrait.jpg" class="image"><img alt="Head and shoulders of man in suit and tie" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/3/35/William_Penney_portrait.jpg/170px-William_Penney_portrait.jpg" width="170" height="275" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/3/35/William_Penney_portrait.jpg/255px-William_Penney_portrait.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/3/35/William_Penney_portrait.jpg/340px-William_Penney_portrait.jpg 2x" data-file-width="396" data-file-height="640" /></a>  <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:William_Penney_portrait.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div><a href="/wiki/William_Penney" class="mw-redirect" title="William Penney">William Penney</a>, Chief Superintendent Armament Research, was in charge of atomic bomb development</div></div></div><p>\nThe Tube Alloys Directorate was transferred from the <a href="/wiki/Department_of_Scientific_and_Industrial_Research_(United_Kingdom)" title="Department of Scientific and Industrial Research (United Kingdom)">Department of Scientific and Industrial Research</a> to the Ministry of Supply effective 1 November 1945.<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEGoldberg1964417_65-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEGoldberg1964417-65">&#91;65&#93;</a></sup> To coordinate the atomic energy effort, Marshal of the Royal Air Force <a href="/wiki/Lord_Portal" class="mw-redirect" title="Lord Portal">Lord Portal</a>, the wartime Chief of the Air Staff, was appointed the Controller of Production, Atomic Energy (CPAE) in March 1946.<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEGowingArnold1974a40\xe2\x80\x9341_66-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEGowingArnold1974a40\xe2\x80\x9341-66">&#91;66&#93;</a></sup> The Gen 75 Committee considered the proposal in October 1946.<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEGowingArnold1974a176\xe2\x80\x93179_67-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEGowingArnold1974a176\xe2\x80\x93179-67">&#91;67&#93;</a></sup> In October 1946, Attlee called a meeting to discuss building a gaseous diffusion plant for <a href="/wiki/Uranium_enrichment" class="mw-redirect" title="Uranium enrichment">uranium enrichment</a>. <a href="/wiki/Michael_Perrin" title="Michael Perrin">Michael Perrin</a>, who was present, later recalled that:</p><style data-mw-deduplicate="TemplateStyles:r856303468">.mw-parser-output .templatequote{overflow:hidden;margin:1em 0;padding:0 40px}.mw-parser-output .templatequote .templatequotecite{line-height:1.5em;text-align:left;padding-left:1.6em;margin-top:0}</style><blockquote class="templatequote"><p>The meeting was about to decide against it on grounds of cost, when <a href="/wiki/Ernest_Bevin" title="Ernest Bevin">[Ernest] Bevin</a> arrived late and said "We\'ve got to have this thing. I don\'t mind it for myself, but I don\'t want any other <a href="/wiki/Secretary_of_State_for_Foreign_and_Commonwealth_Affairs" title="Secretary of State for Foreign and Commonwealth Affairs">Foreign Secretary</a> of this country to be talked at or to by the <a href="/wiki/Secretary_of_State_of_the_United_States" class="mw-redirect" title="Secretary of State of the United States">Secretary of State of the United States</a> as I have just been in my discussion with <a href="/wiki/James_F._Byrnes" title="James F. Byrnes">Mr Byrnes</a>. We\'ve got to have this thing over here, whatever it costs&#160;... We\'ve got to have the bloody <a href="/wiki/Union_Jack" title="Union Jack">Union Jack</a> flying on top of it."<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEBaylisStoddart201532_59-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEBaylisStoddart201532-59">&#91;59&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTECathcart199521_68-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTECathcart199521-68">&#91;68&#93;</a></sup> \n</p></blockquote>\n<p>The decision to proceed was formally made on 8 January 1947 at a meeting of Gen 163, a subcommittee of the Gen 75 Committee consisting of six <a href="/wiki/Cabinet_of_the_United_Kingdom" title="Cabinet of the United Kingdom">Cabinet</a> members, including Attlee,<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEGowingArnold1974a181\xe2\x80\x93184_69-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEGowingArnold1974a181\xe2\x80\x93184-69">&#91;69&#93;</a></sup> and was publicly announced in the <a href="/wiki/House_of_Commons" title="House of Commons">House of Commons</a> on 12 May 1948. <a href="/wiki/D_notice" class="mw-redirect" title="D notice">D notice</a> No. 25 prohibited the publication of details on the design, construction or location of atomic weapons.<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEGowingArnold1974a211\xe2\x80\x93213_70-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEGowingArnold1974a211\xe2\x80\x93213-70">&#91;70&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTECathcart199588\xe2\x80\x9389_71-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTECathcart199588\xe2\x80\x9389-71">&#91;71&#93;</a></sup> The project was given the cover name "High Explosive Research".<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTECathcart199524,_48,_57_72-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTECathcart199524,_48,_57-72">&#91;72&#93;</a></sup> As Chief Superintendent Armament Research (CSAR, pronounced "Caesar"),  Penney directed bomb design from <a href="/wiki/Fort_Halstead" title="Fort Halstead">Fort Halstead</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTECathcart199539\xe2\x80\x9343_73-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTECathcart199539\xe2\x80\x9343-73">&#91;73&#93;</a></sup> In 1951 his design group moved to a new site at <a href="/wiki/Atomic_Weapons_Establishment" title="Atomic Weapons Establishment">Aldermaston</a> in Berkshire.<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEGowingArnold1974b194\xe2\x80\x93196_74-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEGowingArnold1974b194\xe2\x80\x93196-74">&#91;74&#93;</a></sup>\n</p><p>Production facilities were constructed under the direction of <a href="/wiki/Christopher_Hinton,_Baron_Hinton_of_Bankside" title="Christopher Hinton, Baron Hinton of Bankside">Christopher Hinton</a>, who established his headquarters in a former <a href="/wiki/Royal_Ordnance_Factory" title="Royal Ordnance Factory">Royal Ordnance Factory</a> (ROF) at <a href="/wiki/ROF_Risley" title="ROF Risley">ROF Risley</a> in <a href="/wiki/Lancashire" title="Lancashire">Lancashire</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEGowingArnold1974a41_75-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEGowingArnold1974a41-75">&#91;75&#93;</a></sup> These included a uranium metal plant at <a href="/wiki/Springfields" title="Springfields">Springfields</a>,<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEGowingArnold1974b370\xe2\x80\x93371_76-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEGowingArnold1974b370\xe2\x80\x93371-76">&#91;76&#93;</a></sup> nuclear reactors and a plutonium processing plant at <a href="/wiki/Windscale" class="mw-redirect" title="Windscale">Windscale</a>,<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEGowingArnold1974b386_77-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEGowingArnold1974b386-77">&#91;77&#93;</a></sup> and a gaseous diffusion uranium enrichment facility at <a href="/wiki/Capenhurst" title="Capenhurst">Capenhurst</a>, near <a href="/wiki/Chester" title="Chester">Chester</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEGowingArnold1974b430\xe2\x80\x93433_78-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEGowingArnold1974b430\xe2\x80\x93433-78">&#91;78&#93;</a></sup> The two Windscale reactors became operational in October 1950 and June 1951.<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEGowingArnold1974b413\xe2\x80\x93420_79-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEGowingArnold1974b413\xe2\x80\x93420-79">&#91;79&#93;</a></sup> The gaseous diffusion plant at Capenhurst began producing <a href="/wiki/Highly_enriched_uranium" class="mw-redirect" title="Highly enriched uranium">highly enriched uranium</a> in 1954.<sup id="cite_ref-Facilities_80-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Facilities-80">&#91;80&#93;</a></sup>\n</p><p>Uranium ore was stockpiled at Springfields. As the American nuclear programme expanded, its requirements became greater than the production of the existing mines. To gain access to the stockpile, they reopened negotiations in 1947. This resulted in the 1948 <i><a href="/wiki/Modus_Vivendi" class="mw-redirect" title="Modus Vivendi">Modus Vivendi</a></i>,<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEGowingArnold1974a358\xe2\x80\x93360_81-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEGowingArnold1974a358\xe2\x80\x93360-81">&#91;81&#93;</a></sup> which allowed for consultation on the use of nuclear weapons, and limited sharing of technical information between the United States, Britain and Canada.<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEGowingArnold1974a245\xe2\x80\x93254_82-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEGowingArnold1974a245\xe2\x80\x93254-82">&#91;82&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEHewlettDuncan1969281\xe2\x80\x93283_83-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEHewlettDuncan1969281\xe2\x80\x93283-83">&#91;83&#93;</a></sup>\n</p>\n<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Unsuccessful_attempt_to_renew_American_partnership">Unsuccessful attempt to renew American partnership</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Nuclear_weapons_and_the_United_Kingdom&amp;action=edit&amp;section=6" title="Edit section: Unsuccessful attempt to renew American partnership">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>\n<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Op_hurricane.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/9/9c/Op_hurricane.jpg/220px-Op_hurricane.jpg" width="220" height="181" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/9/9c/Op_hurricane.jpg/330px-Op_hurricane.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/9/9c/Op_hurricane.jpg/440px-Op_hurricane.jpg 2x" data-file-width="640" data-file-height="526" /></a>  <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Op_hurricane.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>The UK\'s first nuclear test, <a href="/wiki/Operation_Hurricane" title="Operation Hurricane">Operation Hurricane</a>, in Australia in 1952.</div></div></div>\n<p>By 1949, international control of atomic weapons seemed almost impossible to achieve, and Truman proposed to the <a href="/wiki/Joint_Committee_on_Atomic_Energy" class="mw-redirect" title="Joint Committee on Atomic Energy">Joint Committee on Atomic Energy</a> in July a "full partnership" with Britain in exchange for uranium; negotiations between the two countries began that month. While the <a href="/wiki/Joe_1" class="mw-redirect" title="Joe 1">first Soviet atomic bomb test</a> in August 1949 was embarrassing to the British (who had not expected a Soviet atomic weapon until 1954) for having been beaten, it was for the Americans another reason for cooperation. Although they would soon have their own nuclear capability, the British proposed that instead of building their own uranium-enrichment plant they would send most of their scientists to work in the US, and swap plutonium from Windscale for enriched uranium from the US. While Britain would not formally give up building or researching its own weapons, the US would manufacture all the bombs and allocate some to Britain.<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEBaylis199575\xe2\x80\x9376_84-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEBaylis199575\xe2\x80\x9376-84">&#91;84&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEAldrich1998333\xe2\x80\x93339_85-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEAldrich1998333\xe2\x80\x93339-85">&#91;85&#93;</a></sup>\n</p><p>By agreeing to subsume its own weapons program within the Americans\', the plan would have given Britain nuclear weapons much sooner than its own target date of late 1952. Although a majority of Americans including Truman supported the proposal, several key officials, including the <a href="/wiki/United_States_Atomic_Energy_Commission" title="United States Atomic Energy Commission">United States Atomic Energy Commission</a>\'s <a href="/wiki/Lewis_Strauss" title="Lewis Strauss">Lewis Strauss</a> and Senator <a href="/wiki/Arthur_Vandenberg" title="Arthur Vandenberg">Arthur Vandenberg</a>, did not. Their opposition, along with security concerns raised by the arrest of Fuchs, who was working at Harwell, ended the negotiations in January 1950.<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEDawsonRosecrance196628\xe2\x80\x9329_86-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEDawsonRosecrance196628\xe2\x80\x9329-86">&#91;86&#93;</a></sup> After Britain developed nuclear weapons through its own efforts, the engineer Sir <a href="/wiki/Leonard_Owen" title="Leonard Owen">Leonard Owen</a> stated that "the McMahon Act was probably one of the best things that happened ... as it made us work and think for ourselves along independent lines."<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEGoldberg1964409\xe2\x80\x93429_87-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEGoldberg1964409\xe2\x80\x93429-87">&#91;87&#93;</a></sup>\n</p>\n<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="First_test_and_early_systems">First test and early systems</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Nuclear_weapons_and_the_United_Kingdom&amp;action=edit&amp;section=7" title="Edit section: First test and early systems">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>\n<div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">Main articles: <a href="/wiki/Operation_Hurricane" title="Operation Hurricane">Operation Hurricane</a>, <a href="/wiki/Blue_Danube_(nuclear_weapon)" title="Blue Danube (nuclear weapon)">Blue Danube (nuclear weapon)</a>, and <a href="/wiki/V_bomber" title="V bomber">V bomber</a></div>\n<p>Churchill, now again prime minister, announced on 17 February 1952 that the first British weapon test would occur before the end of the year. During <a href="/wiki/Operation_Hurricane" title="Operation Hurricane">Operation Hurricane</a>, an atomic bomb was detonated on board the <a href="/wiki/Frigate" title="Frigate">frigate</a> <a href="/wiki/HMS_Plym_(K271)" title="HMS Plym (K271)">HMS&#160;<i>Plym</i></a> anchored in a lagoon in the <a href="/wiki/Monte_Bello_Islands" class="mw-redirect" title="Monte Bello Islands">Monte Bello Islands</a> in <a href="/wiki/Western_Australia" title="Western Australia">Western Australia</a> on 3 October 1952.<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEGoldberg1964409\xe2\x80\x93429_87-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEGoldberg1964409\xe2\x80\x93429-87">&#91;87&#93;</a></sup> Britain thereby became the third country to develop and test nuclear weapons.<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEGowingArnold1974b498_88-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEGowingArnold1974b498-88">&#91;88&#93;</a></sup>\n</p>\n<div class="thumb tleft"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Blue_Danube_Bomb.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/en/thumb/9/90/Blue_Danube_Bomb.jpg/220px-Blue_Danube_Bomb.jpg" width="220" height="136" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/en/thumb/9/90/Blue_Danube_Bomb.jpg/330px-Blue_Danube_Bomb.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/en/9/90/Blue_Danube_Bomb.jpg 2x" data-file-width="400" data-file-height="248" /></a>  <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Blue_Danube_Bomb.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>A <i><a href="/wiki/Blue_Danube_(nuclear_weapon)" title="Blue Danube (nuclear weapon)">Blue Danube</a></i> bomb, Britain\'s first nuclear weapon</div></div></div>\n<p>This led to the development of the first deployed weapon, the <a href="/wiki/Blue_Danube_(nuclear_weapon)" title="Blue Danube (nuclear weapon)">Blue Danube</a> free-fall bomb. It had a 60-inch (1,500&#160;mm) diameter, 32 <a href="/wiki/Explosive_lens" title="Explosive lens">explosive lens</a> implosion system with a <a href="/wiki/Levitated_pit" class="mw-redirect" title="Levitated pit">levitated pit</a> suspended within a natural uranium tamper.<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTECathcart1995138\xe2\x80\x93140_89-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTECathcart1995138\xe2\x80\x93140-89">&#91;89&#93;</a></sup> The warhead was contained within a bomb casing measuring 62 inches (1,600&#160;mm) diameter and 24 feet (7.3&#160;m) long, and it weighed approximately 4.5 tonnes (4.4 long tons), of which about 2.5 tonnes (2.5 long tons) was high explosive.<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEAylen201535_90-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEAylen201535-90">&#91;90&#93;</a></sup> The first Blue Danube bombs were delivered to the Royal Air Force (RAF) <a href="/wiki/Bomber_Command" title="Bomber Command">Bomber Command</a> in November 1953,<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEWynn199792_91-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEWynn199792-91">&#91;91&#93;</a></sup> although the bombers to deliver them did not become available until 1955.<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEWynn199755\xe2\x80\x9356_92-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEWynn199755\xe2\x80\x9356-92">&#91;92&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEGowingArnold1974a234\xe2\x80\x93235_93-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEGowingArnold1974a234\xe2\x80\x93235-93">&#91;93&#93;</a></sup>\n</p><p>About fifty-eight Blue Danube bombs were produced.<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEMoore2010112\xe2\x80\x93113,_256_94-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEMoore2010112\xe2\x80\x93113,_256-94">&#91;94&#93;</a></sup> The first bombs had plutonium <a href="/wiki/Pit_(nuclear_weapon)" title="Pit (nuclear weapon)">cores</a>, but all service models were modified to use a composite core which used both uranium-235 and plutonium. The bomb had a yield of 10 to 12 kilotonnes of TNT (42 to 50&#160;TJ).<sup id="cite_ref-95" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-95">&#91;95&#93;</a></sup> The cores were stored separately from the high explosive components in concrete "igloos" at <a href="/wiki/RAF_Barnham" title="RAF Barnham">RAF Barnham</a> in <a href="/wiki/Suffolk" title="Suffolk">Suffolk</a> and <a href="/wiki/RAF_Faldingworth" title="RAF Faldingworth">RAF Faldingworth</a> in <a href="/wiki/Lincolnshire" title="Lincolnshire">Lincolnshire</a>. Some casings were stored elsewhere in the UK and in Cyprus for "second strike" use.<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEAylen201549\xe2\x80\x9350_96-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEAylen201549\xe2\x80\x9350-96">&#91;96&#93;</a></sup> It remained in service until 1962, and was replaced by <a href="/wiki/Red_Beard_(nuclear_weapon)" title="Red Beard (nuclear weapon)">Red Beard</a>, a smaller tactical nuclear weapon. The Blue Danube cores were recycled, and the plutonium used in other nuclear weapons.<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEMoore2010112\xe2\x80\x93113,_256_94-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEMoore2010112\xe2\x80\x93113,_256-94">&#91;94&#93;</a></sup>\n</p><p>Being so big and heavy, Blue Danube could only be carried by the <a href="/wiki/V_bombers" class="mw-redirect" title="V bombers">V bombers</a>,  so-called because they all had names starting with a "V".<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEWynn199756_97-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEWynn199756-97">&#91;97&#93;</a></sup> The three strategic bombers, known collectively as the V class, comprised the United Kingdom\'s strategic nuclear strike force during the 1950s and 1960s, which was known as V force of the Main Force.<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEWynn1997ix,_177_98-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEWynn1997ix,_177-98">&#91;98&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEBrookes1982102,_132_99-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEBrookes1982102,_132-99">&#91;99&#93;</a></sup> The three V bombers were the <a href="/wiki/Vickers_Valiant" title="Vickers Valiant">Vickers Valiant</a>, which entered service in February 1955;<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEWynn1997115_100-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEWynn1997115-100">&#91;100&#93;</a></sup> the <a href="/wiki/Avro_Vulcan" title="Avro Vulcan">Avro Vulcan</a>, which entered service in May 1956; and the <a href="/wiki/Handley_Page_Victor" title="Handley Page Victor">Handley Page Victor</a>, which entered service in November 1957.<sup id="cite_ref-RAF_101-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-RAF-101">&#91;101&#93;</a></sup> The V Bomber force reached its peak in June 1964, when 50 Valiants, 70 Vulcans and 39 Victors were in service.<sup id="cite_ref-102" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-102">&#91;102&#93;</a></sup>\n</p>\n<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Thermonuclear_weaponry">Thermonuclear weaponry</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Nuclear_weapons_and_the_United_Kingdom&amp;action=edit&amp;section=8" title="Edit section: Thermonuclear weaponry">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>\n<div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">Main article: <a href="/wiki/British_hydrogen_bomb_programme" title="British hydrogen bomb programme">British hydrogen bomb programme</a></div>\n<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><div id="mwe_player_0" class="PopUpMediaTransform" style="width:220px;" videopayload="&lt;div class=&quot;mediaContainer&quot; data-height=&quot;360&quot; data-bandwidth=&quot;571048&quot; data-framerate=&quot;29.97002997003&quot;/&gt;&lt;/video&gt;&lt;/div&gt;"><img alt="File:1957-06-03 British H-Bomb (claimed).ogv" style="width:220px;height:165px" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/2/28/1957-06-03_British_H-Bomb_%28claimed%29.ogv/220px-seek%3D18-1957-06-03_British_H-Bomb_%28claimed%29.ogv.jpg" /><a href="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/2/28/1957-06-03_British_H-Bomb_%28claimed%29.ogv" title="Play media" target="new"><span class="play-btn-large"><span class="mw-tmh-playtext">Play media</span></span></a></div>  <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:1957-06-03_British_H-Bomb_(claimed).ogv" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>The <a href="/wiki/Orange_Herald" title="Orange Herald">Orange Herald</a> test on 31 May 1957, claimed to be Britain\'s first H-bomb test at the time, as reported by Universal International Newsreel a few days later. In fact, it was a large fusion-boosted fission weapon test, but the fusion boosting worked very poorly.</div></div></div>\n<p>A month after Britain\'s first atomic weapons test, <a href="/wiki/Ivy_Mike" title="Ivy Mike">America tested</a> the first <a href="/wiki/Thermonuclear_weapon" title="Thermonuclear weapon">thermonuclear (hydrogen) bomb</a>. The Soviets responded with <a href="/wiki/Joe_4" title="Joe 4">Joe 4</a>, a <a href="/wiki/Boosted_fission_weapon" title="Boosted fission weapon">boosted fission weapon</a>, in 1953. Penney believed that Britain could not afford to develop a hydrogen bomb.<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTESpinardi1997547\xe2\x80\x93582_103-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTESpinardi1997547\xe2\x80\x93582-103">&#91;103&#93;</a></sup> Henry Tizard believed that the nation should focus on conventional forces instead of duplicating the nuclear capabilities of the American forces that were already defended Britain and Europe:<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEBaylis199586\xe2\x80\x9387_104-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEBaylis199586\xe2\x80\x9387-104">&#91;104&#93;</a></sup> "We are a great nation, but if we continue to behave like a Great Power we shall soon cease to be a great nation. Let us take warning from the fate of the Great Powers of the past and not burst ourselves with pride."<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEBaylis199586\xe2\x80\x9387_104-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEBaylis199586\xe2\x80\x9387-104">&#91;104&#93;</a></sup>\n</p><p>The <a href="/wiki/First_Sea_Lord" title="First Sea Lord">First Sea Lord</a>, <a href="/wiki/Admiral_(Royal_Navy)" title="Admiral (Royal Navy)">Admiral</a> <a href="/wiki/Louis_Mountbatten,_1st_Earl_Mountbatten_of_Burma" title="Louis Mountbatten, 1st Earl Mountbatten of Burma">Lord Mountbatten</a>, and <a href="/wiki/Chief_of_the_Imperial_General_Staff" class="mw-redirect" title="Chief of the Imperial General Staff">Chief of the Imperial General Staff</a>, <a href="/wiki/General_(United_Kingdom)" title="General (United Kingdom)">General</a> Sir <a href="/wiki/Gerald_Templer" title="Gerald Templer">Gerald Templer</a> supported the development of a hydrogen bomb, but preferred more support for conventional forces. They believed that the large American and Soviet nuclear forces acted as mutual deterrents for nuclear war, making conventional war more likely.<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEBall1995145\xe2\x80\x93147_105-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEBall1995145\xe2\x80\x93147-105">&#91;105&#93;</a></sup> Others proposed that, instead of repeated unsuccessful attempts to increase cooperation with the Americans, Britain work with Australia, Canada, and other Commonwealth countries. Britain could not disclose atomic information to Australia despite testing weapons there because of agreements with the United States.<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEBaylis1995162\xe2\x80\x93163_106-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEBaylis1995162\xe2\x80\x93163-106">&#91;106&#93;</a></sup>\n</p><p>The Chiefs of Staff Committee and the <a href="/wiki/Third_Churchill_ministry" title="Third Churchill ministry">Churchill ministry</a>, however, believed that\n</p>\n<link rel="mw-deduplicated-inline-style" href="mw-data:TemplateStyles:r856303468"/><blockquote class="templatequote"><p>If we did not develop megaton weapons we would sacrifice immediately and in perpetuity our position as a first-class power. We would have to rely on the whim of the United States for the effectiveness of the whole basis of our strategy.<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEBaylis1995145_107-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEBaylis1995145-107">&#91;107&#93;</a></sup>\n</p></blockquote>\n<p>The government decided on 27 July 1954 to begin development of a thermonuclear bomb, and announced its plans in February 1955.<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEBaylis1995160\xe2\x80\x93163,179\xe2\x80\x93185_108-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEBaylis1995160\xe2\x80\x93163,179\xe2\x80\x93185-108">&#91;108&#93;</a></sup> British knowledge of thermonuclear weapons was based on the work done at the Los Alamos Laboratory during the war. Two British scientists, <a href="/wiki/Egon_Bretscher" title="Egon Bretscher">Egon Bretscher</a> and Klaus Fuchs, had attended the conference there on the Super (as it was then called) in April 1946, and Chadwick had written a secret report on it in May 1946,<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEArnoldPyne200138_109-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEArnoldPyne200138-109">&#91;109&#93;</a></sup> but the design was found to be unworkable.<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEBernstein201043\xe2\x80\x9346_110-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEBernstein201043\xe2\x80\x9346-110">&#91;110&#93;</a></sup> Some intelligence about Joe 4 was derived from its debris, which was provided to Britain under the 1948 <i>Modus Vivendi</i>.<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEArnoldPyne200139_111-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEArnoldPyne200139-111">&#91;111&#93;</a></sup> Penney established three megaton bomb projects at Aldermaston: <a href="/wiki/Orange_Herald" title="Orange Herald">Orange Herald</a>, a large boosted fission weapon; <a href="/wiki/Green_Bamboo" class="mw-redirect" title="Green Bamboo">Green Bamboo</a>, an interim thermonuclear design similar to the Soviet Layer Cake used in Joe 4 and the American Alarm Clock; and Green Granite, a true thermonuclear design.<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEArnoldPyne200184\xe2\x80\x9387_112-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEArnoldPyne200184\xe2\x80\x9387-112">&#91;112&#93;</a></sup>\n</p>\n<div class="thumb tleft"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Royal_Engineers_assemble_huts_on_Christmas_Island.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/3/39/Royal_Engineers_assemble_huts_on_Christmas_Island.jpg/220px-Royal_Engineers_assemble_huts_on_Christmas_Island.jpg" width="220" height="168" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/3/39/Royal_Engineers_assemble_huts_on_Christmas_Island.jpg/330px-Royal_Engineers_assemble_huts_on_Christmas_Island.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/3/39/Royal_Engineers_assemble_huts_on_Christmas_Island.jpg/440px-Royal_Engineers_assemble_huts_on_Christmas_Island.jpg 2x" data-file-width="801" data-file-height="612" /></a>  <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Royal_Engineers_assemble_huts_on_Christmas_Island.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>Royal Engineers assemble huts on Christmas Island</div></div></div>\n<p>The Green Granite prototype, known as Short Granite, was tested in the first of the <a href="/wiki/Operation_Grapple" title="Operation Grapple">Operation Grapple</a> test series, Grapple 1. The bomb was dropped from a height of 45,000 feet (14,000&#160;m) by a Vickers Valiant piloted by <a href="/wiki/Wing_commander_(rank)" title="Wing commander (rank)">Wing Commander</a> <a href="/wiki/Kenneth_Hubbard" title="Kenneth Hubbard">Kenneth Hubbard</a>, off the shore of <a href="/wiki/Malden_Island" title="Malden Island">Malden Island</a> in the Pacific on 15 May 1957.<sup id="cite_ref-RAF_Museum_113-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-RAF_Museum-113">&#91;113&#93;</a></sup> It was Britain\'s second airdrop of a nuclear bomb after the <a href="/wiki/British_nuclear_tests_at_Maralinga#Operation_Buffalo" title="British nuclear tests at Maralinga">Operation Buffalo</a> test at <a href="/wiki/Maralinga" title="Maralinga">Maralinga</a> on 11 October 1956, and the first of a thermonuclear weapon.<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEArnoldPyne2001139_114-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEArnoldPyne2001139-114">&#91;114&#93;</a></sup> The United States had not attempted an airdrop of a hydrogen bomb until the <a href="/wiki/Operation_Redwing" title="Operation Redwing">Operation Redwing</a> Cherokee test on 21 May 1956.<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEArnoldPyne200121_115-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEArnoldPyne200121-115">&#91;115&#93;</a></sup> Short Granite\'s yield was estimated at 300 kilotonnes of TNT (1,300&#160;TJ), far below its designed capability.<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEArnoldPyne2001145\xe2\x80\x93146_116-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEArnoldPyne2001145\xe2\x80\x93146-116">&#91;116&#93;</a></sup> Despite its failure, the test was hailed as a successful thermonuclear explosion, and the government did not confirm or deny reports that the UK had become a third thermonuclear power.<sup id="cite_ref-117" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-117">&#91;117&#93;</a></sup> When documents on the series began to be declassified in the 1990s, they were denounced as a hoax.<sup id="cite_ref-118" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-118">&#91;118&#93;</a></sup> The reports were unlikely to have fooled the American observers.<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEBaylis1994171_119-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEBaylis1994171-119">&#91;119&#93;</a></sup>\n</p><p>The next test was Grapple 2, of Orange Herald,<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEHubbardSimmons2008142\xe2\x80\x93146_120-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEHubbardSimmons2008142\xe2\x80\x93146-120">&#91;120&#93;</a></sup> the first British weapon to incorporate an <a href="/wiki/External_neutron_initiator" class="mw-redirect" title="External neutron initiator">external neutron initiator</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEMcIntyre200628_121-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEMcIntyre200628-121">&#91;121&#93;</a></sup> It was dropped on 31 May,<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEHubbardSimmons2008142\xe2\x80\x93146_120-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEHubbardSimmons2008142\xe2\x80\x93146-120">&#91;120&#93;</a></sup> and exploded with a force of 720 to 800 kilotonnes of TNT (3,000 to 3,300&#160;TJ). The yield was the largest ever achieved by a single stage device,<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEMcIntyre200629\xe2\x80\x9330_122-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEMcIntyre200629\xe2\x80\x9330-122">&#91;122&#93;</a></sup> which made it technically a megaton weapon.<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEArnoldPyne2001147_123-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEArnoldPyne2001147-123">&#91;123&#93;</a></sup>  The bomb was hailed as a hydrogen bomb, and the truth that it was actually a large fission bomb was kept secret by the British government until the end of the <a href="/wiki/Cold_War" title="Cold War">Cold War</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEDombeyGrove19928\xe2\x80\x939_124-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEDombeyGrove19928\xe2\x80\x939-124">&#91;124&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEBaylis1994167\xe2\x80\x93168_125-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEBaylis1994167\xe2\x80\x93168-125">&#91;125&#93;</a></sup> Penney cancelled the planned Green Granite test, and substituted Purple Granite, a Short Granite with some minor modifications.<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEArnoldPyne2001145\xe2\x80\x93146_116-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEArnoldPyne2001145\xe2\x80\x93146-116">&#91;116&#93;</a></sup> Its yield was a very disappointing 300 kilotonnes of TNT (1,300&#160;TJ), even less than Short Granite; the changes had not worked.<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEArnoldPyne2001147_123-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEArnoldPyne2001147-123">&#91;123&#93;</a></sup>\n</p><p>An <a href="/wiki/Operational_Requirement" title="Operational Requirement">Operational Requirement</a> (OR1142) was issued in 1955 for a thermonuclear warhead for a <a href="/wiki/Medium-range_ballistic_missile" title="Medium-range ballistic missile">medium-range ballistic missile</a>, which became <a href="/wiki/Blue_Streak_(missile)" title="Blue Streak (missile)">Blue Streak</a>. This was revised in November 1955, with "megaton" replacing "thermonuclear". Orange Herald could then meet the requirement.<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEMcIntyre200626\xe2\x80\x9327_126-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEMcIntyre200626\xe2\x80\x9327-126">&#91;126&#93;</a></sup> Codenamed <a href="/wiki/Green_Grass_(nuclear_warhead)" class="mw-redirect" title="Green Grass (nuclear warhead)">Green Grass</a>, the unsuccessful fusion boosting was omitted, and it used Green Bamboo\'s 72-lens implosion system instead of Orange Herald\'s 32. This allowed the amount of highly enriched uranium to be reduced from 120 to 75&#160;kg. Its yield was estimated at 0.5 megatonnes of TNT (2.1&#160;PJ).<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEMcIntyre200629\xe2\x80\x9330_122-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEMcIntyre200629\xe2\x80\x9330-122">&#91;122&#93;</a></sup> It was placed in a Blue Danube casing, and became known as <a href="/wiki/Violet_Club" title="Violet Club">Violet Club</a>.
